data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> -7,5%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: ASSAEROPORTI<sup id="cite_ref-assaeroporti.it_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assaeroporti.it-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from Assaeroporti<sup id="cite_ref-Assaeroporti_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Assaeroporti-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Milan Malpensa Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>MXP</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LIMC</b>) is the largest <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Milan_metropolitan_area" title="Milan metropolitan area">Milan metropolitan area</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>. It serves around 17 million inhabitants in <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>, as well as those living in the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Ticino" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton of Ticino">Canton of Ticino</a>. The airport is located 49 kilometres (30&#160;mi) northwest<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> of central <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, next to the <a href="/wiki/Ticino_(river)" title="Ticino (river)">Ticino</a> river (dividing Lombardy and Piedmont). The airport has two <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminals</a> (Terminal 1 and Terminal 2) and two <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> as well as a dedicated cargo terminal.\n</p><p>In 2019, Malpensa Airport handled 28,846,299 passengers and was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">20th busiest airport in Europe in terms of passengers</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Italy" title="List of the busiest airports in Italy">2nd busiest airport in Italy in terms of passengers</a>. Until 2008, Malpensa Airport was a major <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>. Malpensa Airport remains the second-busiest Italian airport for international passenger traffic (after <a href="/wiki/Rome_Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Fiumicino Airport">Rome Fiumicino Airport</a>), and the busiest for freight and cargo, handling over 500,000 tons of international freight annually.\n</p><p>The first industrial airport was opened in 1909 near the Cascina Malpensa, an old farm, by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Agusta" title="Giovanni Agusta">Giovanni Agusta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Caproni" class="mw-redirect" title="Gianni Caproni">Gianni Caproni</a> to test their aircraft prototypes. This airport was then opened for civil operation in 1948 during the war reconstruction period, in order to serve the northern area of Milan.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" view</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The site of today\'s Malpensa Airport has seen aviation activities for more than 100 years. The first began on 27 May 1910, when the Caproni brothers flew their "flying machine", the Cal biplane. In the years that followed, many aircraft prototypes took off from the same site; eventually, it was decided to upgrade the farming patch to a more formal airfield. Both Gianni Caproni and Giovanni Agusta established factories on the new site; the airfield soon developed into the largest aircraft production centre in Italy.\n</p><p>During the 1920s and 1930s, the airfield hosted two squadrons of the <i>Regia Aeronautica Italiana</i> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_Air_Force" title="Italian Air Force">Italian Air Force</a>). In September 1943, Malpensa airfield was taken over by Nazi Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> when northern Italy was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. Soon after their arrival, the Germans laid the airfield\'s first concrete runway.\n</p><p>After the cessation of hostilities during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, manufacturers and politicians of the Milan and Varese regions, led by banker Benigno Ajroldi of Banca Alto Milanese, restored the airfield. They aimed to make it an industrial fulcrum for post-war recovery of Italy. The main runway, heavily damaged by German troops as they retreated from northern Italy, was rebuilt and extended to 1,800 metres. A small wooden terminal was constructed to protect goods and passengers from bad weather.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_World_War_II">After World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: After World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Malpensa Airport officially commenced commercial operations on 21 November 1948 as <i>Aeroporto Citt\xc3\xa0 di Busto Arsizio</i>, although the Belgian national flag-carrier <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a> had started flying to <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> from here a year earlier. On 2 February 1950 <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a> (TWA) became the first company to fly long-haul flights from Malpensa, using <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Constellation" title="Lockheed Constellation">Lockheed Constellations</a> on their services to New York <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">Idlewild Airport</a> (now JFK).\n</p><p>A change of ownership occurred in 1952 when the Municipality of <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> took control of the airport\'s operator, the <i>Societ\xc3\xa0 Aeroporto di Busto Arsizio</i>. The operator\'s name was subsequently changed to <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Societ%C3%A0_Esercizi_Aeroportuali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Societ\xc3\xa0 Esercizi Aeroportuali (page does not exist)">Societ\xc3\xa0 Esercizi Aeroportuali SpA</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Societ%C3%A0_Esercizi_Aeroportuali" class="extiw" title="it:Societ\xc3\xa0 Esercizi Aeroportuali">it</a>&#93;</span></i> (SEA). After assuming full control, SEA decided to develop Malpensa as an international and intercontinental gateway, whereas Milan\'s other airport, <a href="/wiki/Linate_Airport" title="Linate Airport">Linate Airport</a>, would be tasked with handling only domestic services.\n</p><p>Between 1958 and 1962 a new terminal arrived at Malpensa and the airport\'s two parallel runways were extended to 3,915&#160;m (12,844&#160;ft), becoming the longest in Europe at that time. By the early 1960s, however, major European carriers such as <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> had moved the majority of their services to Linate Airport, which was just 11&#160;km east of Milan\'s city centre, making it much easier for passengers to reach central Milan. This left Malpensa with just a handful of intercontinental links, charter flights and cargo operations. Malpensa suffered a decline in commercial traffic, with passenger numbers dropping from 525,000 in 1960 to just 331,000 by 1965. It was destined to play second fiddle to Linate Airport for another 20 years.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Expansion_and_development_.281995.E2.80.931998.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_development_(1995\xe2\x80\x931998)">Expansion and development (1995\xe2\x80\x931998)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expansion and development (1995\xe2\x80\x931998)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By the mid-1980s Linate Airport was handling seven million passengers per year and, with only a short single runway and limited parking slots, had reached its saturation point. With no available land nearby for expansion, an alternative solution was sought: <i>Societ\xc3\xa0 Esercizi Aeroportuali SpA</i> (SEA) quickly found that developing Malpensa was the only practical alternative.\n</p><p>By the end of 1985, a law had been passed by the Italian Parliament that paved the way for the reorganisation of the Milan airport system. Malpensa was designated as the centre for all services covering northern Italy, while Linate Airport was downgraded to a domestic and short-haul facility. "Malpensa 2000", as the plan was called, included the construction of a new terminal as well as the development of fast, efficient connections to Milan\'s city centre. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> recognised this project as one of the 14 "Essential to the Development of the Union" and provided \xe2\x82\xac200 million to help finance the work. Construction started in November 1990; Malpensa airport was re-opened eight years later.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="A_brief_life_as_Alitalia.27s_main_hub_.281998.E2.80.932008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="A_brief_life_as_Alitalia\'s_main_hub_(1998\xe2\x80\x932008)">A brief life as Alitalia\'s main hub (1998\xe2\x80\x932008)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: A brief life as Alitalia&#039;s main hub (1998\xe2\x80\x932008)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the night of 24/25 October 1998, <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> moved the majority of its fleet from <a href="/wiki/Rome_Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Fiumicino Airport">Rome Fiumicino Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 where it had been flying from for over 50 years \xe2\x80\x93 to Malpensa Airport. The airport started a new lease of life as the Italian flag carrier\'s main hub. Alitalia added up to 488 movements and 42,000 passengers a day at the facility which, by the end of 1998, had handled 5.92 million passengers (an increase of more than two million over the previous year\'s figure).\n</p><p>In 1999 it recorded a spectacular leap to 16.97 million and, by 2007, passenger numbers had reached 23.9 million. Efficient rail links from two different stations in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Milano_Centrale_railway_station" title="Milano Centrale railway station">Centrale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milano_Cadorna_railway_station" title="Milano Cadorna railway station">Cadorna</a> stations) ensured easy access by railway, whereas the nearby <a href="/wiki/Autostrada_A8_(Italy)" title="Autostrada A8 (Italy)">A8 motorway</a> had an extra lane added in each direction to help speed up traffic into and out of the city centre.\n</p><p>Before 2001, ground handling services at <a href="/wiki/Malpensa" class="mw-redirect" title="Malpensa">Malpensa</a> were shared by the SEA (airport\'s operator) and Trans-World Airlines. Since then, the contracting process has gradually been deregulated. In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Airport_security" title="Airport security">airport security</a> services at Malpensa were transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Polizia_di_Stato" title="Polizia di Stato">Polizia di Stato</a> (State Police) to SEA\'s internal division, SEA Airport Security. Up to 2002, SEA was assisted by IVRI in providing security services, but the contract was not renewed after its expiry. Nevertheless, SEA Airport Security is supervised by the Polizia di Stato (Italian State Police), <a href="/wiki/Guardia_di_Finanza" title="Guardia di Finanza">Guardia di Finanza</a> (Italian Military Customs Police) and Ente Nazionale Aviazione Civile (Italy\'s Civil Aviation Authority), whereas the <a href="/wiki/Carabinieri" title="Carabinieri">Carabinieri</a> (Italian Military Police) supervises ramp entrance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Ramp services are provided by SEA Handling, ATA and, more recently, Aviapartner. SEA Handling provided 80% of the ramp services at Malpensa Airport due to its major customer, <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>. In May 2006, however, Italy\'s Civil Aviation Authority took off the limitation of two ramp handlers.\n</p><p>In 2008, a new development plan was launched by <i>Societ\xc3\xa0 Esercizi Aeroportuali SpA</i> (SEA), valued at \xe2\x82\xac1.4 billion, to include a third pier for Terminal 1 and the construction of a third runway. In a surprise move, however, Alitalia announced its decision to revert to <a href="/wiki/Rome_Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Fiumicino Airport">Rome Fiumicino Airport</a> as its main hub, due to \'high operating costs\' at Malpensa Airport. Alitalia did not pull out of Malpensa altogether and continues to fly several domestic and European services from Milan and two intercontinental flights (to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>). However, Malpensa lost around 20% of its daily movements, a decrease from 700 to 550, which resulted in only 19.2 million passengers passing through in 2008. The airport continued to suffer during 2009 when the international financial crisis and higher fuel prices caused a reduction to only 17.6 million passengers that year.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_expansion:_2010s">Recent expansion: 2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Recent expansion: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Responding to Alitalia\'s pullout, the operator SEA launched an all-out publicity programme and aggressively marketed Malpensa Airport around the world. This campaign was successful: from 2008 to 2011, a total of 34 new passenger and cargo routes were added to Malpensa\'s network.\n</p><p>The low-cost carrier <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> made Malpensa its main base after <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick</a>, with more than 20 of its <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320s</a> based there. The airline currently flies services from Malpensa to more than 70 destinations in Italy and across Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Competitor <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> confirmed plans to open an operating base at Malpensa from December 2015, initially with one aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014 a contract was awarded for extension of the railway line from Terminal 1 to Terminal 2. The line was opened in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The new Malpensa Terminal 2 railway station is within 200 m north of the T2 arrivals hall, that is accessed by an outdoor covered walkway.<sup id="cite_ref-new-t2-station_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-t2-station-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg/220px-EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg/330px-EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg/440px-EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="766" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EasyJet_Airbus_A319_Pierobon-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319-100">Airbus A319-100</a> landing at Malpensa with the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> visible in the background</div></div></div>\n<p>Malpensa Airport has two passenger terminals and they are connected by airport shuttle buses and trains.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 1, which opened in 1998, is the newer,<sup id="cite_ref-Avventure_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avventure-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> larger and more prominent terminal. The terminal is divided into three sections and handles most passengers on scheduled as well as charter flights:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Terminal 1A</b> handles domestic and intra-<a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen</a> flights.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 1B</b> handles non-Schengen and intercontinental flights.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 1C</b>, opened in January 2013, handles non-Schengen, intercontinental flights and security-sensitive flights to USA and Israel.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 2 is the older terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-Avventure_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avventure-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It is currently used exclusively by <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>. All <a href="/wiki/Charter_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter airline">charter services</a>, which were previously based in this terminal, moved to Terminal 1 upon its opening.\n</p><p>Malpensa Airport additionally provides free shuttles connecting Terminal 2 to Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled, seasonal and charter flights to and from Malpensa:<sup id="cite_ref-auto_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">Riga</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/AlbaStar" title="AlbaStar">AlbaStar</a> </td><td><b>Seasonal: </b><a Wikidata query and sources</a>.</small>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_links">Transport links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Aeroporto_Terminal_1_railway_station" title="Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 1 railway station">Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 1 railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Aeroporto_Terminal_2_railway_station" title="Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 2 railway station">Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 2 railway station</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg/220px-Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg/330px-Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg/440px-Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malpensa_Express_at_Milano_Cadorna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Malpensa Express at Milan Cadorna station platform 1</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malpensa_Gallery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Malpensa_Gallery.jpg/220px-Malpensa_Gallery.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Malpensa_Gallery.jpg/330px-Malpensa_Gallery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Malpensa_Gallery.jpg/440px-Malpensa_Gallery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malpensa_Gallery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Connection between Terminal 1 and its railway station</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport is served by two train stations, one in each terminal.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malpensa_Express">Malpensa Express</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Malpensa Express">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Express" title="Malpensa Express">Malpensa Express</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Express" title="Malpensa Express">Malpensa Express</a> is a direct train connection between <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Aeroporto_Terminal_2_railway_station" title="Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 2 railway station">Terminal 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_Aeroporto_Terminal_1_railway_station" title="Malpensa Aeroporto Terminal 1 railway station">Terminal 1</a> and Milan\'s city center.\n</p><p>As of 2019, its service is based on a <a href="/wiki/Clock-face_scheduling" title="Clock-face scheduling">clock-face</a> timetable with four services per hour in both directions: two run between the two airport terminals and <a href="/wiki/Milano_Cadorna_railway_station" title="Milano Cadorna railway station">Milan Cadorna</a> station; the other two between the two airport terminals, <a href="/wiki/Milano_Porta_Garibaldi_railway_station" title="Milano Porta Garibaldi railway station">Milan Garibaldi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milano_Centrale_railway_station" title="Milano Centrale railway station">Milan Centrale</a> stations. All services call at <a href="/wiki/Busto_Arsizio_Nord_railway_station" title="Busto Arsizio Nord railway station">Busto Arsizio Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saronno_railway_station" title="Saronno railway station">Saronno</a> (connections for <a href="/wiki/Como" title="Como">Como</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novara" title="Novara">Novara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Varese" title="Varese">Varese</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Milano_Bovisa_railway_station" title="Milano Bovisa railway station">Milan Bovisa</a> stations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The journey time ranges between 30 and 50 minutes, depending on the type of service and number of stops.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_train_services">Other train services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other train services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Treni_Regionali_Ticino_Lombardia" title="Treni Regionali Ticino Lombardia">TiLo</a> operate services to <a href="/wiki/Bellinzona_railway_station" title="Bellinzona railway station">Bellinzona</a> in Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Milan\'s Suburban Line <b>S10</b> (Milano Rogoredo\xe2\x80\x93Milano Bovisa) ran to Malpensa Airport/Aeroporto from June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Trains call at: Ferno, Busto Arsizio, Castellanza, Rescaldina, Saronno, Milano Bovisa, Milano Lancetti, Milano Porta Garibaldi <a href="/wiki/Milan_Metro_Line_2" title="Milan Metro Line 2">M2</a>-<a href="/wiki/Milan_Metro_Line_5" title="Milan Metro Line 5">M5</a>, Milano Repubblica <a href="/wiki/Milan_Metro_Line_3" title="Milan Metro Line 3">M3</a>, Milano Porta Venezia <a href="/wiki/Milan_Metro_Line_1" title="Milan Metro Line 1">M1</a>, Milano Dateo and Milano Porta Vittoria. The service was terminated in October 2012.\n</p><p>The Malpensa \xe2\x80\x93 Varese \xe2\x80\x93 Mendrisio (CH) \xe2\x80\x93 Lugano (CH) line provides a direct connection between Malpensa Airport/Aeroporto and the south-eastern part of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>. There are plans to connect Gallarate Station and Milan\'s Centrale Station (FS), which is currently a terminus station with no through tracks, to allow more convenient access to high-speed international lines.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>Malpensa Shuttle</b> and <b>Malpensa Bus Express</b> connect the airport to <a href="/wiki/Milano_Centrale_railway_station" title="Milano Centrale railway station">Milan Central station</a> (<a href="/wiki/Trenitalia" title="Trenitalia">Trenitalia</a>\'s National Railway hub) and for Milan\'s Metro network. The shuttle bus calls at Terminals 1 and 2, Busto Arsizio and Milan Fair (on request). Journey time is 60\xe2\x80\x9370 minutes.</li>\n<li>A free, 24-hour shuttle bus provides access to Terminal 2 from Terminal 1. The bus leaves every 7 minutes. Journey time is 15\xe2\x80\x9320 minutes.</li>\n<li>Malpensa Airport has a direct coach connection with Milan\'s <a href="/wiki/Linate_Airport" title="Linate Airport">Linate Airport</a>.</li>\n<li>From March 2018 both Terminals are connected to major cities in Northern Italy. This service is provided by <b>BusItalia Fast</b> (a society participated by Trenitalia and the Italian Rail Co.) and connects the airport with <a href="/wiki/Aosta" title="Aosta">Aosta</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">Aosta Valley</a>), <a href="/wiki/Novara" title="Novara">Novara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santhi%C3%A0" title="Santhi\xc3\xa0">Santhi\xc3\xa0</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sanremo" title="Sanremo">Sanremo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savona" title="Savona">Savona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ventimiglia" title="Ventimiglia">Ventimiglia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>) once a day; <a href="/wiki/Padua" title="Padua">Padua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venice_Marco_Polo_Airport" title="Venice Marco Polo Airport">Venice Marco Polo Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a> (<a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a>), <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> (<a href="/wiki/Friuli-Venezia_Giulia" class="mw-redirect" title="Friuli-Venezia Giulia">Friuli-Venezia Giulia</a>) twice a day; <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>) three times a day.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Milan_Malpensa_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Malpensa Airport is accessible by a four-lane motorway to the <a href="/wiki/Autostrada_A8_(Italy)" title="Autostrada A8 (Italy)">A8</a> (connecting Switzerland to Milan) and by a five-lane motorway to the <a href="/wiki/Autostrada_A4_(Italy)" title="Autostrada A4 (Italy)">A4</a> (connecting Turin/Torino, Verona, Venice and Triest/Trieste). Local access to the airport is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Strada_statale_336_dell%27Aeroporto_della_Malpensa" title="Strada statale 336 dell&#39;Aeroporto della Malpensa">State Road SS336</a> from <a href="/wiki/Busto_Arsizio" title="Busto Arsizio">Busto Arsizio</a> and by the State Road SS336dir from <a href="/wiki/Magenta,_Lombardy" title="Magenta, Lombardy">Magenta</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span
